  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9a93127e-38b4-41d2-8a74-ae498d9d4374'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5639077603308768087">THE TOUCHING TRUE STORY THAT WON THE HEARTS OF MILLIONS OF READERS AROUND THE WORLD!<br/><br/>Anna was only four years old when Fynn found her on London's fog-shrouded docks. He took her back to his mother's home, and from that first moment, their times together were filled with delight and discovery. Anna had an astonishing ability to ask--and to answer--life's largest questions. H</span>
  <span id="freeText5639077603308768087" style="display:none">THE TOUCHING TRUE STORY THAT WON THE HEARTS OF MILLIONS OF READERS AROUND THE WORLD!<br /><br />Anna was only four years old when Fynn found her on London's fog-shrouded docks. He took her back to his mother's home, and from that first moment, their times together were filled with delight and discovery. Anna had an astonishing ability to ask--and to answer--life's largest questions. Her total openness and honesty amazed all who knew her. She seemed to understand with uncanny certainty the purpose of being, the essence of feeling, the beauty of love. You see, Anna had a very special friendship with Mister God. . . .</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_205077').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/389933389" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7583770-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338980644p2/7583770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/389933389?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/7583770-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006245636" href="/book/show/1678897.Mister_God_This_is_Anna">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer389933389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11621404771216075787">Five stars are not enough. So I am going to take my "mirror book" and create an endlessly repeating circle of stars. Anna deserves no less.<br/><br/>This is a spiritual and philosophical book, but it is not tied into religion. Anna is spectacularly, terrifyingly and completely ALIVE!Every fibre of her being hums and sparks with life, feeling and imagination. <br/><br/>What makes me sad about reading this again after almost 30 years is the realisation that I have become so full of holes. This became obvious when the</span>
  <span id="freeText11621404771216075787" style="display:none">Five stars are not enough. So I am going to take my "mirror book" and create an endlessly repeating circle of stars. Anna deserves no less.<br /><br />This is a spiritual and philosophical book, but it is not tied into religion. Anna is spectacularly, terrifyingly and completely ALIVE!Every fibre of her being hums and sparks with life, feeling and imagination. <br /><br />What makes me sad about reading this again after almost 30 years is the realisation that I have become so full of holes. This became obvious when the little nagging voice in my head insisted that the relationship between Fynn and Anna was odd. It's really not. Anna and Fynn loved each other. They fully trusted and believed in each other. It's a sign of how jaded I've become that I doubted the purity of that feeling for even a moment.<br /><br />This book is like night-time: "It stretches your soul right out to the stars. And that...is a very long way."</span>
  <a data-text-id="11621404771216075787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_425605081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425605081" />
    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2533794-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343779895p2/2533794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425605081?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/2533794-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2533794-vivian?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2533794-vivian?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425605081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8670393110124742132">As I began reading this I was prepared to dismiss it as a cheap attempt by "anonymous" to challenge the accepted philosophy and practices of Christianity. It begins with a teenage dock worker, Fynn, in pre-WWII London finding an abandoned four-year-old girl one night and taking her home to his mother. Over the next several years the girl, whom they call Anna, fills his life with wonder and his mind with her ideas about "Mister God". How, I wondered, could this young man have the quantity of idle</span>
  <span id="freeText8670393110124742132" style="display:none">As I began reading this I was prepared to dismiss it as a cheap attempt by "anonymous" to challenge the accepted philosophy and practices of Christianity. It begins with a teenage dock worker, Fynn, in pre-WWII London finding an abandoned four-year-old girl one night and taking her home to his mother. Over the next several years the girl, whom they call Anna, fills his life with wonder and his mind with her ideas about "Mister God". How, I wondered, could this young man have the quantity of idle time he appears to spend with this girl AND work AND study math and science AND read philosophy and classics to the extent he says he does. He has a microscope and a slide rule and he assembles a radio set. In short, he does not fit with the neighborhood he describes nor the person he professes to be.<br /><br />I was sufficiently troubled about all this to execute some google searching. Searching the word "Fynn", I found: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mister_God,_This_Is_Anna">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mister_G...</a><br />Searching the phrase "Mister God, This is Anna", I found: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mister_God,_This_Is_Anna">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mister_G...</a> but best of all this link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.finchden.com/sgh/index.htm">http://www.finchden.com/sgh/index.htm</a> My skepticism was satisfied and I was able to read the remainder of the book with a more open mind.<br /><br />There are some thoughts in the book that did not resonate with me, but much that did. In fact, so much so that I began reading aloud full chapters to various members of my family and enjoying the passages even more with each reading. Anna has the capacity to think out of the box, so to speak, because she has never been fettered with a box. Fynn is something of a child prodigy himself when it comes to all things mathematical. The combination of the two produces some amazing theories about metaphysics and Christianity.<br /><br />This is by no means a sentimental, trite, or simple story, as the title might suggest to today's reader. In fact, I intend to re-read parts of it and add reference notes in my copy of the book. As a whole it is beyond amazing. It is astounding.<br /><br />Post script: This story is also an exploration about a revolutionary model of the education process. Ideally, all children would be more like Anna, and perhaps they are. In which case, providing MORE time for idle wanderings, tinkering, and engaging in the scientific process combined with discussion, questioning, postulating, framing solutions by the child and extensive reading of the classics and immersion in acquired areas of interest and expertise by teens and adults with the same eagerness as the child would result in a more invigorating and effective educational process. Three cheers for Anna and Fynn!!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8670393110124742132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Honest writing is a really rare find nowadays but this book, despite convention, remains, even if untrue, honest. <br/><br/> </span>

<div id="review_676065594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676065594" />
    <a title="Dan Glover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3120943-dan-glover"><img alt="Dan Glover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571348931p2/3120943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/676065594?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Glover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Glover" href="/user/show/3120943-dan-glover">Dan Glover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006245636" href="/book/show/1678897.Mister_God_This_is_Anna">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3120943-dan-glover?shelf=theology-church-discipleship">theology-church-discipleship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3120943-dan-glover?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer676065594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16081262717133939216">I read this book quite a while ago. It is engagingly written but it contains some very errant and very wishful thinking theology. The story centers around the relationship between a 4-7 year old girl (story takes place over 3 years) and a 16-19 year old boy who finds her on the street one night and brings her home to his mother. The girl lives with them over the next three years and the "action", in so far as it happens (and not much of it does) is basically just to give context for Fynn and Ann</span>
  <span id="freeText16081262717133939216" style="display:none">I read this book quite a while ago. It is engagingly written but it contains some very errant and very wishful thinking theology. The story centers around the relationship between a 4-7 year old girl (story takes place over 3 years) and a 16-19 year old boy who finds her on the street one night and brings her home to his mother. The girl lives with them over the next three years and the "action", in so far as it happens (and not much of it does) is basically just to give context for Fynn and Anna's conversations about life and the nature of God. Anna sees God as her mentor and personal teacher but the church and Scripture don't factor in. Anna teaches Fynn that God is in everyone and everyone is in God. As I mentioned, the book is fairly well written but the content is really just a hybrid form of pantheistic universalism. The narrative plays on your emotions all the way along until the tear-jerking finish, with Anna dying in a tragic accident (this is not a spoiler as the narrator makes you aware of this very near the beginning of the book). The book is often billed as a Christian book, but the true gospel is not presented in any way and much that runs directly contradictory to Scripture is, along with the emotional manipulation to sway you to believe it. I could not recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16081262717133939216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_887603998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/887603998" />
    <a title="Faith Spinks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7125008-faith-spinks"><img alt="Faith Spinks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348529033p2/7125008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/887603998?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith Spinks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith Spinks" href="/user/show/7125008-faith-spinks">Faith Spinks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006245636" href="/book/show/1678897.Mister_God_This_is_Anna">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125008-faith-spinks?shelf=biographies">biographies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125008-faith-spinks?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125008-faith-spinks?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer887603998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17276249849858512656">This book is so very, very beautiful. It is simple and yet profound. It is a book that I have read, re-read and re-read again and again. And I never tire of it. Every time I read it I discover some new gem. My copy of the book makes it an art to read as it is beyond the 'falling apart' stage. The pages are no longer attached and yet for me that is just a sign of how loved the book is. Loved by my parents and then passed on and loved by me.<br/><br/>I never met Anna, but I feel like I have, and I like her.</span>
  <span id="freeText17276249849858512656" style="display:none">This book is so very, very beautiful. It is simple and yet profound. It is a book that I have read, re-read and re-read again and again. And I never tire of it. Every time I read it I discover some new gem. My copy of the book makes it an art to read as it is beyond the 'falling apart' stage. The pages are no longer attached and yet for me that is just a sign of how loved the book is. Loved by my parents and then passed on and loved by me.<br /><br />I never met Anna, but I feel like I have, and I like her. I like her a lot! Anna was just four years old when Fynn found her wandering round London’s Docklands one foggy night in the 1930s. Badly neglected and abandoned by her parents, he took her home to be cared for by his own family. She was little and she was young but her impact by far outsized her. Nobody who met Anna remained the same: not even Bossy the cat or Patch the dog who she tamed in an instant. As Fynn said of her, "this was no casual knowing; it required total application." Anna may have been young but she was an intelligent, lively, precocious chatterbox who had an outlook on life which could completely transform your understanding of life and make you think "of course it is that simple!" <br /><br />One of the things about Anna is the incredible relationship she had with 'Mister God'. Not some distant childhood vision of a god sitting on a throne up in the clouds, but in her wonderful matter of fact way she just really knew 'Mister God'. And her insights were just incredible. And as you read you find yourself, along with Fynn, learning so much. Anna's mirror book, her understanding that you can do billions of sums when you start with the answer, the way she could see everyday objects in a way which reflected her understanding of 'Mister God' are just some of the amazing aspects of Anna. <br /><br />Each time I read it I feel like I come away having gleaned more than from any sermon, or from all my years at school. On this reading one of the things that struck me was the understanding that God's greatest creative act was rest. He spent 6 days sorting out the muddle that was there in the first place and then to crown it all he created rest for us. "When he finished making all things, Mister God had undone the muddle. Then you can rest, so that's why rest is the very, very biggest miracle of all." God didn't rest at the end of all that creating because he was tired. Of course not. He's God! He created rest!<br /><br />Anna dies before she even reaches her eighth birthday and yet at the end of the book I put it down with a sense of feeling full, of wonder and of gratitude for the life she lived and the impact she made. "Anna's life hadn't been cut short, far from it, it had been full, completely fulfilled"<br /><br />Anna’s influence continues today. Anyone reading this dips into her thought-processes, and then you can't help but fall under the wonder of her innocence, wisdom and amazing relationship with ‘Mister God’. Read it, and see what your eyes get opened to!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17276249849858512656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_325350645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325350645" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7201609-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/325350645?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/7201609-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer325350645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8550335922539367665">True story of a 4-year-old found on the streets of London in the 1930's by a 19-year<br/>old blue collar worker with a passion for math and music and all things mechanical. <br/>The first edition included the tale of how the book's manuscript came into the hands <br/>of the publisher and of a meeting with "Fynn," the book's author; all subsequent <br/>editions have omitted it.<br/>Anna had an intimate relationship with "Mister God," and searched for him in all things.<br/>Everything and everyone in creation was evidence for </span>
  <span id="freeText8550335922539367665" style="display:none">True story of a 4-year-old found on the streets of London in the 1930's by a 19-year<br />old blue collar worker with a passion for math and music and all things mechanical. <br />The first edition included the tale of how the book's manuscript came into the hands <br />of the publisher and of a meeting with "Fynn," the book's author; all subsequent <br />editions have omitted it.<br />Anna had an intimate relationship with "Mister God," and searched for him in all things.<br />Everything and everyone in creation was evidence for Anna that God existed, that he was<br />a gentleman, and that he loved people in ways they could not possible comprehend. She<br />prayed for the gift of asking "real questions" and to avoid those which led nowhere.<br />Theology has been a lifelong passion for me; Anna is my favorite theologian. Her ideas<br />resonate with the child inside me - her fearless trust, her refusal to accept adult<br />explanations based on fear, her spirit afire with love of God. I have probably given<br />away 25 or more copies of this book; people are often daunted by the explanations in the<br />language of math and mechanics. I can only say look beyond; look at Anna's love; look<br />at the relationship between Anna and Fynn. Smile at their willingness to turn the world<br />upside down and see God everywhere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8550335922539367665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_63634910" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63634910" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2526106-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557331096p2/2526106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63634910?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2526106-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345327222" href="/book/show/860697.Mister_God_This_Is_Anna">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jason by: </span>
      Michael McCamish
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2526106-jason?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2526106-jason?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2526106-jason?shelf=new-age">new-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63634910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8117716940145936504">The book recounts the friendship formed between the author and narrator Fynn (who is in his late teens or early 20s in the narrative) and a foundling named Anna in London's East End, in the 1930s. Anna, reminiscent of a character from Dickens, is a little girl who lives on the streets until she is taken in by the narrator. She has a unique perspective on life, a mystical spirituality, and a boundless curiosity that she shares with the author and the reader on every page. She occasionally (at lea</span>
  <span id="freeText8117716940145936504" style="display:none">The book recounts the friendship formed between the author and narrator Fynn (who is in his late teens or early 20s in the narrative) and a foundling named Anna in London's East End, in the 1930s. Anna, reminiscent of a character from Dickens, is a little girl who lives on the streets until she is taken in by the narrator. She has a unique perspective on life, a mystical spirituality, and a boundless curiosity that she shares with the author and the reader on every page. She occasionally (at least once per chapter) lets loose with a metaphor or pronouncement that is as deep as they come, but it is hard to imagine a real five-year old spouting these profundities with such regularity. Was she a real kid or just a figment of the author's imagination? I have no idea, but I do know that her death in the final chapter (this isn't a spoiler---Fynn tells us about her death in the first few pages) felt real enough.<br /><br />I loved the characters of Fynn and Anna, yet I have mixed feelings about the book itself. It was given to me as a gift by a good friend, who in turn had it recommended to him. Both recommendations came with the suggestion that the book had substantially shifted their perspectives. Yet in reading the book, I could never shake my suspicion that the author was just using sentimental tricks to make the book seem profounder than it really was. (It felt like the same kind of emotional manipulation that I associate with the movie <i>Forrest Gump</i>.) Put it this way: if the wise-sounding comments had come from an adult, rather than from a small homeless child, would they still have seemed as deep?<br /><br />Luckily, the book is an easy read and is readily available in almost every thrift store in the country, so you can read it for yourself and see what you think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8117716940145936504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1469085866" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469085866" />
    <a title="Ziggy Zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23992175-ziggy-zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie"><img alt="Ziggy Zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442626948p2/23992175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1469085866?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ziggy Zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ziggy Zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie" href="/user/show/23992175-ziggy-zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie">Ziggy Zezsyazeoviennazabrizkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006278917" href="/book/show/935303.Mister_God_This_is_Anna">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469085866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17531270212367375602">I gave 4 stars, but I'm gonna rant a bit. Well, several paragraphs.<br/><br/>I read the 1979 edition, and first and foremost, I was very much entertained by the preface by Vernon Sproxton. V. Sproxton categorized this book as an 'Ah!' book. A book beyond good, that is. Well I personally won't put this book in 'beyond-good' category. Not because it's not well-written--it is--but I have different shelves. I put this book on 'thinking book' category. Easy enough, it's one of those books that got you thinking</span>
  <span id="freeText17531270212367375602" style="display:none">I gave 4 stars, but I'm gonna rant a bit. Well, several paragraphs.<br /><br />I read the 1979 edition, and first and foremost, I was very much entertained by the preface by Vernon Sproxton. V. Sproxton categorized this book as an 'Ah!' book. A book beyond good, that is. Well I personally won't put this book in 'beyond-good' category. Not because it's not well-written--it is--but I have different shelves. I put this book on 'thinking book' category. Easy enough, it's one of those books that got you thinking; not necessarily because it has novel premises or extraordinary originality, but it makes you think just because.<br /><br />Speaking of premises, this book is full of theological ideas, simplified by character Anna. It's not baffling for me, so that's not the 'thinking' part. Anna was.<br /><br />This book, in its good intention, attempts to exploit the wisdom of a child. That is, seeing certain delicate matter from much more innocent, blunt perspective that, once polished, can be insightful. Here's where I got baffled: Can I qualify Anna as a child? Sure, she still brought childlike quality in her character--inventing words, stubbornness and persistence, bluntness and such. But her thinking process is uncanny. Not bothered with her grasp in science and math, nor over her devotion to God. But her capacity to relate the two--translating the concept of God into everyday words--is surreal. Not saying it's impossible, but it sure is implausible. I myself relate concrete things to abstract concepts on daily basis, but the earliest attempt was perhaps at age 7 at best, and it's not polished or anywhere nearing presentable. Anna's fluency in wrapping her thoughts and presenting it in her easy ways isn't something quite childlike. Again, not impossible, just making the character Anna artificial and hard to relate to.<br /><br />Another thing is, Anna was described in such way that made her too close to being Mary Sue. But when thought over, that's only how the narrator saw her. If you put her in real-life, you'll meet an insufferable know-it-all who corresponds only to people who'd accept her points, and actually quite an attention seeker too. I did sympathize with Anna at first, her being quite beaten up and somewhat astray. But if it's read through, tho many people around her liked her, many people didn't too.<br /><br />And that's where it struck me: this book was narrated by a person who loved, admired, and was devoted to Anna so much it didn't make sense that she's anything but flawless. And also, it's written in memory of a dead person. It's so easy for living person to only recollect good memories, or polish bad ones, when reminiscing a dead person. That's why, Anna is not a child. Not really. She's a dead girl in memory of a grown up, jumbled and got mixed up in an adult's insights. That's why thoughts presented by Anna in this book is not wholly her own; it's probably merely a superficial childish thoughts translated and edited by a grown-up's comprehension in attempt to make her something poetic. Anna's an impression; a learning media, a tool, a cover; but not really a child.<br /><br />So, talking about the grown-up behind Anna. Some people are bugged by the relationship between Anna and Fynn. Understandable. Very. I mean, had the story been fast-forwarded to many years and Anna's a living teen, there's gonna be some romantic notion in the development. I can accept that two people can develop relationship that is not at all romantic, but Anna and Fynn's certainly is not one of them. Here's why: the word 'delicious' is not is not is not a proper word to be paired with a child. I got goosebumps every time the word's used to describe Anna. And the way their physical interaction was described is too intimate. Anna's kisses might be childish, so were her hand-holding, head-resting, hugging, and stuff; but the depiction didn't sound that innocent. So I'm sort of under impression that, not only did Fynn admire Anna, he's somewhat obsessed by her. Not in good way, if there's any.<br /><br />But anyway, it's not a bad book. Not at all, actually. When I realized that this book's created by someone in memory of a dead, I decided that this book's captivating in how sensible and real did it capture this certain situation. Also, I like how they think of God and all divine stuff--that's how I see religion thingy as well. And the book is amazingly capable of explaining those perspective in very simple, straightforward way that it became so easy to understand. The narration is very well-written, and it had childlike quality itself. That is, none of its words was constructed for quotation purpose; if there's anything anyone can quote, it's just a happy accident, not intentional. That's why it sounds honest, and that's why it's so enjoyable to read.<br /><br />And the ending is touching and dramatic. Anna's death--wouldn't say it's a spoiler, since the death of Anna is already there at the beginning of things--was tragic and real; the accident she fell into was one that any kid could've been in. Although, Anna's bit on facing her own death was quite too theatrical. But Fynn's reaction was redeeming. It seemed to be very natural, everything on how he tried to deal with Anna's death. I love the ending because of him. There's a closure, a resolution, and an air of new beginning; in short, a peaceful and fresh way to end a story.<br /><br />It's started and ended with death, but this book is about living. Getting closer to Christmas, I say it's an amazing, heart-warming read for them good Christian who wants to read something about God that has nothing to do with Santa and sleigh ride. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17531270212367375602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer1152000411586732762">Mister God, This is Anna is a book a bout a man who finds a little girl wandering the streets, and he takes her home. This always tickles me, because: how insane! Granted it does sort of explain itself out of that hole, and the book is set in the 1930s so it is forgivable, but still, it makes me giggle.   <span id="freeText1152000411586732762" style="display:none">Mister God, This is Anna is a book a bout a man who finds a little girl wandering the streets, and he takes her home. This always tickles me, because: how insane! Granted it does sort of explain itself out of that hole, and the book is set in the 1930s so it is forgivable, but still, it makes me giggle. Then again, if you pulled that kind of thing today, would anyone notice? I think it's probably less likely than we expect. <br /><br />Anyway, the book is ok, I suppose. I don't think you need to be a believer in God to enjoy it, you simply need to be respectful of religion, I suppose. Anna is a precocious little thing who spends her days puzzling the narrator, Fynn, with intense questions and poignant observations about the world around her. It does get a bit blahblahblah in the middle, but all-in-all it is quite a sweet story. </span>

<div id="review_1534555568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1534555568" />
    <a title="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all"><img alt="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406361683p2/20738920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1534555568?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" href="/user/show/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all">Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=absolute-favourites">absolute-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=1920s-1930s">1920s-1930s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=thinking-people-s-books">thinking-people-s-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1534555568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer254954468401278279">I remember when the American paperback edition of this book came out in the 1970s and all of the adults in my parents' immediate circle jumped on it. I must have been about 13 when I got my hands on it and read it and loved it. Unlike Fynn and Anna, I've never understood math, partly thanks to being forced into "the new math" at age 8 and missing three vital years of basic arithmetic, and then transferring to a school that had never taught the new math, realising kids my age needed the old one m</span>
  <span id="freeText254954468401278279" style="display:none">I remember when the American paperback edition of this book came out in the 1970s and all of the adults in my parents' immediate circle jumped on it. I must have been about 13 when I got my hands on it and read it and loved it. Unlike Fynn and Anna, I've never understood math, partly thanks to being forced into "the new math" at age 8 and missing three vital years of basic arithmetic, and then transferring to a school that had never taught the new math, realising kids my age needed the old one more. I never had a slide rule (and the people around me don't even know what it is these days) or a piano or even an oscilliscope, but their adventures sure sounded like fun. I read it several times, stole my parents' copy when I went off to college and moved to Europe, and finally lost it at about age 30 when I lent it to someone who left the country without returning it. <i>(Which is sorta OK, because we had traded books and I borrowed her copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9375.Fried_Green_Tomatoes_at_the_Whistle_Stop_Cafe" title="Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistle Stop Cafe by Fannie Flagg" rel="nofollow noopener">Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistle Stop Cafe</a>. I would have returned it, but she left no adress, and this was in the days before the Internet, where I live now.)</i><br /><br />Fast forward to the 90s, and I came across a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50811.Anna_and_the_Black_Knight" title="Anna and the Black Knight by Fynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the Black Knight</a> and pounced on it. Read it, but found it less about Mr God and more about math and physics. It also made me wonder; the main characters in Fynn's books all seem to have a habit of dying at the end. <br /><br />Just recently, due to a GR friend reading "Mr God", I ordered a copy of the Anna trilogy and re-read the first book. And the older, more cynical me wonders still: Was Anna a real person, or a device that Fynn used to float his ruminations on reality, mathematics, spirituality and so on? I know that in 1930s London there were many street kids who basically floated through life--Fynn himself seems to have been one, after a fashion, as he was first a student and then a staff member of a "therapeutic community" according to Wikipedia and a website called "therealfynn.co.uk." I haven't read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50808.Anna_s_Book" title="Anna's Book by Fynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna's Book</a> yet, which purports to be notes and jottings written by Anna herself, so the jury's still out on that one. <br /><br />If Anna was real, and she had lived, she would probably have been a math or science whizkid, and as that plus an idealist plus a woman, at that time in that place probably would have been a misfit and quite unhappy. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="254954468401278279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_254975559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254975559" />
    <a title="BetteRose Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4815634-betterose-ryan"><img alt="BetteRose Ryan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254975559?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BetteRose Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BetteRose Ryan" href="/user/show/4815634-betterose-ryan">BetteRose Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254975559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10923775539955085705">A book I loved, loved, loved when I first read it in the late 1970's. It is one of those books that stays with you for decades. .<br/><br/>The book allows us to meet Anna, a precocious child of four years. She has run away from home and makes a life with Fynn and his mum. During her short life, Anna develops a refined way of looking at almost everything around her and manages to teach twenty year old Fynn a thing or two about life. From the moment Anna refused to tell anyone where her parents lived to the</span>
  <span id="freeText10923775539955085705" style="display:none">A book I loved, loved, loved when I first read it in the late 1970's. It is one of those books that stays with you for decades. .<br /><br />The book allows us to meet Anna, a precocious child of four years. She has run away from home and makes a life with Fynn and his mum. During her short life, Anna develops a refined way of looking at almost everything around her and manages to teach twenty year old Fynn a thing or two about life. From the moment Anna refused to tell anyone where her parents lived to the moment of her death, Anna manages to control her environment and those around her, although her control is a loving, gentle control.<br /><br />Anna treats Fynn with her special philosophy of church, God, sex, and numbers. The reader is taken along for this wonderful ride.<br /><br />My Take:<br />This is a short book I want everyone to read, though there are some who will find it too simple to enjoy. I loved Anna and her many ideas. One of my favorites is when Anna realized she knew the answer to a squillion (the biggest number Anna could think of) questions. Just when Fynn thinks he is going to set her right, she proves she is already right: How much is 4 take away 1? How much is 2 plus 1? How much is 5 take away 2? By now you must have figured out we could go on all day with this line of reasoning. Indeed, Anna taught Fynn that it is the questions that are truly important. Even beyond that, it is the circumstance of the question that is important. Saying yes to the offer of a drink of water may be drastically different depending on if you are three days into the desert or just newly arrived at the restaurant.<br /><br />There are some who say this child could not have just come to live with this family, It did happen in the 1930's and having little children run the streets was not unheard of. There are some who may say no child could ever do or think what Anna did but I am here to tell you, I personally know of at least one. And don't forget Mozart wrote music at this same age and played his sister's violin without being taught at this same age or younger.<br /><br />I highly recommend this little treasure!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10923775539955085705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_963993143" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/963993143" />
    <a title="Borum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15410264-borum"><img alt="Borum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562163411p2/15410264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/963993143?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Borum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Borum" href="/user/show/15410264-borum">Borum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer963993143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7083889767235929382">As I read this book I kept having this image of Anna as not a little girl of five, but a tiny version of Socrates deeply emerged in a Platonic dialogue or Jesus enlightening both his ignorant enemies and followers in one of his allegorical parables. <br/><br/>Although the prose is relatively simple and somewhat coarse in some parts of the book and Anna's explanations are rough and terse even to the point of being abtruse, it just goes to show you that not all beauty is created by skilled and stylish techn</span>
  <span id="freeText7083889767235929382" style="display:none">As I read this book I kept having this image of Anna as not a little girl of five, but a tiny version of Socrates deeply emerged in a Platonic dialogue or Jesus enlightening both his ignorant enemies and followers in one of his allegorical parables. <br /><br />Although the prose is relatively simple and somewhat coarse in some parts of the book and Anna's explanations are rough and terse even to the point of being abtruse, it just goes to show you that not all beauty is created by skilled and stylish techniques of trained artists and not all truth lies in fanciful and coherent arguments. Just as Jesus lied in the manger and Buddah among the ragged, sometimes the most beautiful poetry and the deepest, truest philosophy is 'in the middle' of a field of wildflowers, a child's indecipherable scribble or the silent smile of the common prostitute. In fact, this book eventually goes to demonstrate that when you're 'full' inside, you don't need to fret about what's outside or peripheral, you can concentrate on what's 'in the middle' and being 'what I am' and Mister God. <br /><br />This book, of course, is not for everyone. I wouldn't recommend it to people who don't want to be turned 'inside out' and keep being confined inside the box they built around themselves. I also don't think this is a book for people who think that math is just math and physics is just physics. It is for those who vaguely suspect that 2 and 2 might not always be four and are on a lifetime search for not only answers but also for questions that landed somewhere and answers that all questions are headed for. It is also for those who long for many others that sing in the same chord yet are often confounded by the different names of the chord. It is for those who wish to be step across the borders of knowledge and senses, but be liberated with imagination, wit and compassion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7083889767235929382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1815616491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987336-sarah?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987336-sarah?shelf=religion">religion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1815616491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8740085376277549085">Out of the mouths of babes, indeed! The tale of a truly remarkable little girl and the impact of her short life. Were this a work of fiction I would have found young Anna an unbelievable character. Beyond precocious, Anna is deep and preceptive. Her observations and revelations, particularly those involving her view on Mister God, blew me away. Many times I had trouble following her line of thought and had to work my own lil' noggin in order to grasp the meaning she was trying to convey.<br/>To moder</span>
  <span id="freeText8740085376277549085" style="display:none">Out of the mouths of babes, indeed! The tale of a truly remarkable little girl and the impact of her short life. Were this a work of fiction I would have found young Anna an unbelievable character. Beyond precocious, Anna is deep and preceptive. Her observations and revelations, particularly those involving her view on Mister God, blew me away. Many times I had trouble following her line of thought and had to work my own lil' noggin in order to grasp the meaning she was trying to convey.<br />To modern American sensibilities the relationship between this man and the child he discovers late one night are odd, to be sure. But, that was part of the book's charm. It forced me to set aside my preconceived notions about childcare and focus instead on the content of their relationship rather than the parameters. I will definitely be checking out Fynn's further musings about Anna.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8740085376277549085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer95330292" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15425019391652446619">This is one of two books that perfectly encapsulates my view of the world and life. Anna sees everything around her in terms of God, but not the frowning, disappointed God that so many small people use as a means of judging others. Anna's God is so big that he is practically beyond our perception of emotions, in the way that an ant cannot comprehend the vastness of the picnickers on the grass. Anna brings God down out of the subconsciously-assumed clouds of Heaven and places Him solidly in the r</span>
  <span id="freeText15425019391652446619" style="display:none">This is one of two books that perfectly encapsulates my view of the world and life. Anna sees everything around her in terms of God, but not the frowning, disappointed God that so many small people use as a means of judging others. Anna's God is so big that he is practically beyond our perception of emotions, in the way that an ant cannot comprehend the vastness of the picnickers on the grass. Anna brings God down out of the subconsciously-assumed clouds of Heaven and places Him solidly in the reality of prostitutes, balloons, and music, to name just a few vessels. Her God is truly omniscient because he is truly omnipresent, seeing His creation from every possible angle. All this insight from an eight year old girl from London's East Side.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15425019391652446619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8259165416599807416">I am Anna. <br/>Or I thought I was, when I was 10 years old and reading that book. I also thought I had secret magic powers back then. This book helped my self esteem, I guess. I would give it a two, had I not seen myself in the protagonist. But it is really moving in many ways. And, even now, when I see the title on my bookshelf, it takes me back to an age I believed endless possibilities were lying ahead of me.</span>

<div id="review_339499231" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339499231" />
    <a title="Shutterbug_iconium" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2908970-shutterbug-iconium"><img alt="Shutterbug_iconium" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272810860p2/2908970.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339499231?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shutterbug_iconium" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shutterbug_iconium" href="/user/show/2908970-shutterbug-iconium">Shutterbug_iconium</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345289100" href="/book/show/935304.Mister_God_This_Is_Anna">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shutterbug_iconium by: </span>
      A friend
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339499231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17178453462031156227">Anna, age five and physically abused runs from home and is on the street. Finn accidentally meets him on the streets and this is the story of their a few year old friendship. Anna is just so intelligent. She's beyond normal reckoning. The philosophy she develops about God, the insight she displays into theological stuff will surely stay with me.<br/><br/>The book reminded me of Eric-Emmanuel Schmitt's Oscar and the Lady in Pink, which chronicles the the letters of a terminally ill boy of ten addressed to </span>
  <span id="freeText17178453462031156227" style="display:none">Anna, age five and physically abused runs from home and is on the street. Finn accidentally meets him on the streets and this is the story of their a few year old friendship. Anna is just so intelligent. She's beyond normal reckoning. The philosophy she develops about God, the insight she displays into theological stuff will surely stay with me.<br /><br />The book reminded me of Eric-Emmanuel Schmitt's Oscar and the Lady in Pink, which chronicles the the letters of a terminally ill boy of ten addressed to God. Anna and Oscar may not necessarily resemble each other but they way they walk about God is so humorous and sometimes moving.<br /><br />“Do you believe in God?”<br />“Yes.”<br />“Do you know what God is?”<br />“Yes.”<br />“What is God then?”<br />“He’s God.”<br />“Do you go to church?”<br />“No.”<br />Why not?<br />“Because I know it all.”<br />“What do you know?”<br />“I know to love Mister God and to love people and cats and dogs and spiders and flowers and trees – and the catalogue went on- with all of me.”<br /><br />For Anna, God is a being who goes beyond any religion or rules. At four years old, Anna knows that being aware of the existence of God and following him is not about complying with some strict rules or attending church sessions. Anna puts it in a wonderfully simple way that loving one another is supposed to be more important than anything else for anyone. For Anna, if you did not really get this message, then church-going is "just for swank."<br />Instead of taking for granted what God wants men to do, where he is or how big his love is, Anna tries to philosophize about God and find some decent answers. At six, she is the theologian, mathematician,philosopher, and poet more than anyone else. She doesn't expect to find clear-cut,direct answers. She just knows an answer would lead to another bigger question because God,unlike what most people thought, Mister God could be any size he wanted to be.<br />If Fynn enriched this story by introducing more characters, more diverse dialogues and a better plot, I would have liked the book more I guess. From the beginning to the end, you are supposed to read either the dialogues between them or what Finn makes of them and that honestly spoils the fun.<br /><br />P.S I got this book on betterworldbooks.com It's written Henderson Library Lon Morris College on it. The name of the previous owner is crossed out. I wish they could just leave that name there:(<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17178453462031156227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_711308797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711308797" />
    <a title="Jeske" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11816872-jeske"><img alt="Jeske" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585500104p2/11816872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711308797?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeske" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeske" href="/user/show/11816872-jeske">Jeske</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11816872-jeske?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11816872-jeske?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11816872-jeske?shelf=christianity">christianity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11816872-jeske?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11816872-jeske?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11816872-jeske?shelf=auto-biographies-true-stories">auto-biographies-true-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711308797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7403586204792047461">Wonderful book about a beautiful friendship between a teenager and a little girl who found each other in their search for the questions to important answers. Recommendation for everyone who is not afraid to have his core ideas on God, humanity, love and life shaken quite a bit and then transformed into honest, frolicky and tender child-logic. (which often proves to be rationally better logic than that of us heavily conditioned grownups). One simply cannot escape the beautiful usage of words and </span>
  <span id="freeText7403586204792047461" style="display:none">Wonderful book about a beautiful friendship between a teenager and a little girl who found each other in their search for the questions to important answers. Recommendation for everyone who is not afraid to have his core ideas on God, humanity, love and life shaken quite a bit and then transformed into honest, frolicky and tender child-logic. (which often proves to be rationally better logic than that of us heavily conditioned grownups). One simply cannot escape the beautiful usage of words and the endearing description of Anna, the wise and sensitive little girl you will fall in love with without a doubt. <br /><br />Some quotes:<br /><br />'You see, Fynn, people can only love outside and can only kiss outside, but Mister God can love you right inside and mister God can kiss you right inside, so it's different. Mister God ain't like us; we are a little bit like Mister God, but not much yet.'<br /><br />***<br /><br />'Fynn, that's the difference. You see, everybody has got a point of view, but mister God hasn't. Mister God has only points TO view.'<br />Humanity has an infinite number of points of view. God has an infinite number of viewing points. That means that God is everywhere.<br /><br />***<br /><br />People can't talk about Mister God from the outside; you can only talk about Mister God from the inside of Him.<br /><br />***<br /><br />'Fynn, you know that book about four dimensions?'<br />'yes, what about it?'<br />'I know where number four is; it goes right inside me.'<br /><br />***<br /><br />Later that afternoon, while we were sitting on the grass eating chocolate, she said, 'Them words.'<br />'What words?' I asked.<br />'Them words that say to keep off the grass - them words are like that church we went to this morning.'<br />Then it all became apparent. Like the flower-beds the church service had been to Anna nothing less than a notice saying 'Keep off the grass'. She couldn't get at the best bits. To be inside a church, not at a church service, but simply to be inside, was for Anna like visiting a very, very special friend, and visiting a very special friend is a happy occasion, and that, surely, is a good enough reason to dance. Inside a church Anna danced; it was the best bit. Church services, therefore, like the 'Keep off the grass' notices, did not allow her to have the best bit. I smiled as i pictured the kind of service that Anna would have liked. I'm not so sure that Mister God wouldn't have preferred it too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7403586204792047461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141944932" />
    <a title="Nelly Ivanova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2492261-nelly-ivanova"><img alt="Nelly Ivanova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293665199p2/2492261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141944932?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nelly Ivanova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nelly Ivanova" href="/user/show/2492261-nelly-ivanova">Nelly Ivanova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141944932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16873955800711275698">Толкова просто поднесени мъдрости, че умът не го побира. <br/><br/>'Tich,' I said, 'what were you asking God about real questions for?'<br/>'Oh, it's just sad, that's all.'<br/>'What's sad?'<br/>'People is.'<br/>'I see. What's sad about people?'<br/>'People ought to get more wise when they grow older. Bossy and Patch do, but people don't.'<br/>'Don't you think so?'<br/>'No. People's boxes get littler and littler.'<br/>'Boxes? I don't understand that.'<br/>'Questions are in boxes,' she explained, 'and the answers they get only fit the size of the box</span>
  <span id="freeText16873955800711275698" style="display:none">Толкова просто поднесени мъдрости, че умът не го побира. <br /><br />'Tich,' I said, 'what were you asking God about real questions for?'<br />'Oh, it's just sad, that's all.'<br />'What's sad?'<br />'People is.'<br />'I see. What's sad about people?'<br />'People ought to get more wise when they grow older. Bossy and Patch do, but people don't.'<br />'Don't you think so?'<br />'No. People's boxes get littler and littler.'<br />'Boxes? I don't understand that.'<br />'Questions are in boxes,' she explained, 'and the answers they get only fit the size of the box.'<br />'That's difficult; go on a bit.'<br />'It's hard to say. It's like - it's like the answers are the same size as the box. It's like them dimensions.'<br />'Oh?'<br />'If you ask a question in two dimensions, then the answer is in two dimensions too. It's like a box. You can't get out.'<br />'I think i see what you mean.'<br />'The questions get up to the edge and then stop. It's like a prison.'<br />'I expect we're all in some sort of prison.'<br />She shook her head. 'No. Mister God wouldn't do that.'<br />'I suppose not. What's the answer then?'<br />'Let Mister God be. He lets us be.'<br />'Don't we?'<br />'No. We put Mister God into little boxes.'<br />'Surely we don't do that?'<br />'Yes, all the time. Because we don't really love him. We got to let Mister God be free. That's what love is.'</span>

<div id="review_17428441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17428441" />
    <a title="Jeanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/931861-jeanne"><img alt="Jeanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203687342p2/931861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17428441?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanne" href="/user/show/931861-jeanne">Jeanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17428441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8739808131788322409">I've had this one on the bookshelf for a log time. Someone must have recommended it because it's not a book I would probably pick out on my own. <br/><br/>So far it's okay. There are a few illustrations thrown in there and I could do without those, they're horrible. I am not really a fan of Fynn, the male character in this book. The relationship between Anna and Fynn is a bit weird too. <br/><br/>I'll keep trudging on...<br/><br/>update: It's starting to pick up around page 90 (isn't that too far along for a book to pick up?</span>
  <span id="freeText8739808131788322409" style="display:none">I've had this one on the bookshelf for a log time. Someone must have recommended it because it's not a book I would probably pick out on my own. <br /><br />So far it's okay. There are a few illustrations thrown in there and I could do without those, they're horrible. I am not really a fan of Fynn, the male character in this book. The relationship between Anna and Fynn is a bit weird too. <br /><br />I'll keep trudging on...<br /><br />update: It's starting to pick up around page 90 (isn't that too far along for a book to pick up?). <br /><br />The character Anna made me think of a Brian Andreas quote-<br /><br />"She said she usually cried at least once each day not because she was sad, but because the world was so beautiful &amp; life was so short"<br /><br />update- i have pretty much given up on this book..it just sits on my night stand, lonely. i read some reviews of this book as i wondered if i was the only one who disliked this book. turns out, yup, i'm one of very few. i *get* the book, i get the gist of it, i understand the message being relayed, the point of view and perspective...i just hate the way it was delivered.<br /><br />another update- i picked it up again. at least i finished it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8739808131788322409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_480204719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/480204719" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/323130-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188492019p2/323130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/480204719?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/323130-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer480204719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17781883954606008639"><i>It doesn’t really matter what color you are, what creed you subscribe to; Mister God shows no preference in his function.</i><br/><br/>This quote is one of many in this thought-provoking book that deserves to be pondered, highlighted, discussed, or jotted down in notebooks designated for favorite quotes from favorite books. I chose this quote rather specifically for my review because it is a quote that succinctly sums up the reason why I like this book. Ultimately, this book is about faith, and this quote (mo</span>
  <span id="freeText17781883954606008639" style="display:none"><i>It doesn’t really matter what color you are, what creed you subscribe to; Mister God shows no preference in his function.</i><br /><br />This quote is one of many in this thought-provoking book that deserves to be pondered, highlighted, discussed, or jotted down in notebooks designated for favorite quotes from favorite books. I chose this quote rather specifically for my review because it is a quote that succinctly sums up the reason why I like this book. Ultimately, this book is about faith, and this quote (more so than the 20 to 30 others I could have chosen) best sums up my own definition of faith. <br /><br />So. . .there you have it. I liked this book because I have never before ever seen such a close approximation to my own personal definition of faith in print. Three stars allotted because the book itself is somewhat of a throw away to me; I read it and moved on to something else. But if I didn’t already believe in the sentiments posited forth by this work, then it would have gotten a full five stars. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17781883954606008639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KTRRkMdknnl9butd4kN9J8vl7osoHnCcEWHIsiSH3/JmkutYVE7U/Qqh3AgS0b2Ey+F4CsM0Nfbe2AsojqtZ4g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BmIEf2vnewIcJpzzBoVwbaPp0cNrwRyqcOdkzkh0Y51JxL63+M0xhmvpq6b2F7DOo+1HQoDrWcC/XqdU4ljljQ==')})
  }
